*	In the Comments: <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj_mwPQpfm_sdwpms-2xCI4yaTNlB4jfELWe9-zPdQfYkfvAUol3H6lQ9n80bkT_-xfqw_44A3BM2F6WO3QGOqGHoOc0kK6o5QnmeqlXTg9abcmxok-Wv4mPQnOJStlFkJzpi0eT4Emvryw8RO7zTWPEyaGngNwjPocryjdGz3yBtDgyE2X1TFcVcatZ8Lq5jkU=>  "Forcing DSP's to get seat-level permission for every advertiser slows down the flow of programmatic buying and limits auction pressure, keeping prices flat. (visit AdExchanger.com)

Yahoo! Responds Publicly

Ad Age's Jason Del Ray talks to Yahoo! head of North American sales Wayne Powers about DSPs, retargeters and ad networks (oh my!) and precluding them from buying Yahoo! owned and operated remnant display inventory through Right Media Exchange (RMX). Powers doesn't mince words, "When arbitragers come in and get access to your inventory, no one is happy. Advertisers are paying a lot more than if they bought direct and we're not happy when people position themselves as representing our company." Read more about Yahoo! taking  <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj8QidOjzP1ksKF74SkuV1FlN8F-AsAA_wkhjNbuu_Aca3OY8nb25wF0_wXigH6xWwrA2eK7cmauQB6cIYh-JksWkLfxCtR7dGEVD6hoNXkh2EHj_XE1qSC8pV5ej5iY3CSU6w2XYgCWF0B-E82zJuaPkMN4oh1YNUzUW8iVG88-gK22o7FZqczot2XsqfZ1Ml0w42-T99ENNrX0-5ss89LfZTSg9mF7LRg=> "Full Ownership." 


DFP Mobile Ad Serving

On AdMonsters, Google's DFP Product Manager Marcel Gordon talks mobile ad serving in an interview. Gordon explains the cross-channel strategy, "We don't think about DFP Mobile as a mobile ad server; rather, DFP is an ad server that understands mobile from the ground up. Mobile campaigns run on the same ad serving platform that DFP provides for desktop." Read it all <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj9x14S-ulBatOc2uSTYkASa0tt0mcBeBn5xcN1SXTDSoDeowcek4MRtcLvgrS2Rl3SBppnP8qtU-ceV5YX5NbJ5x53VpnpKblJ47vZMN6n7FUne_Gx7eQITlbdJEYO9_Iy6d8UoEfY9W-s7bGLFL1E_0ZljlfhTBUleVdOunLuQd3MHzngohSd8FD-PsjYAuMus1-5GFTFrOg==> . Fueled by complexity from numerous formats and devices, as well as the fact its just plain early in mobile, mobile ad serving is one area that still seems up for grabs as startups continue to provide alternatives. 


Publishers, Agencies And Yahoo!

On his personal blog, VivaKi's Marco Bertozzi takes note of the evolution in the digital landscape and the Yahoo! DSP move. He sees implications for agencies, "It is refreshing to see the strategy Yahoo is playing out in the US. (...) They are going to take a hit in the US with their strategy of blocking the Ad Nets, Criteos and others from buying their inventory. Yes short term that is going to hurt them, longer term its a great move and will pay back undoubtedly. (...) Agencies are evaluating just as fast, less from a revenue perspective, more from a structural perspective." Bertozzi then looks at key trends for publishers and agencies. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj8eD1_O81YotYQRqOBy1gzrRFfTE1qEXn6hjueeW_-YCnh0o2zrkwDGexCLwqsYlSAN_qO7NLeg4G7TJlIxI2Dy8mtoWFA_sH27DrQMhTYBAZv5-NnsDtxLflB9L8m4nkA4NKoS2U9f-HPODcsxcZRE2NO_x1N8kkHdrQtLBDOaa4S3IJXwYPzWRzJnB-V16go=>  


Ruminating On The GRP

On ClickZ, Media Contacts account director Jessica Richards offers her view on the GRP for video. (There should be a big tug of war about the online GRP - real ropes - do it up right.) She's for the GRP and says, "In my opinion, the major changes in the future will need to be standardization. More and more pricing models have extended to allow for buying on GRPs or full video views to make digital more accountable. As the digital technology becomes more interchangeable with traditional media, the metrics will need to change to encompass a holistic view of overall results, whether traditional TV or any form of digital video." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj8ipJ1evs2IMI83Hi-yLAwk14H45IiMQIJeAAKIn_9oADt-FpdpHn4sszsZubdvfMC0Py4RduR2lEwDWY9_woJ630g0BkI5KnoLZUyKDMI-oUT750OCuDZE4wMze1WzXh2Zt3MY99EsQ9MmmFZNfkxr312EbtpgKSBTk5nLkBruRQ==>  


Technology Is Worth It

On Digiday, MediaMath's Joe Zawadzki offers more views on Yahoo! and its remnant display strategy. He tells Digiday's Carla Rover about the impact on advertisers: "What is sometimes lost in these discussions is that 'optimization is not zero sum.' That is, a technology that improves results by 100 percent and charges 20 percent is a fantastic bargain." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj-IQzXaLo60bZzAHKUw_de3I5A792pyHFFXJ4bIoMkg5HmsgdcnGmgY_NnTrNVUXMmX61MnkdEMLEwxSOEUxR_QD_Yf06JngChTcx4jXlDkkQpB0jES_JvMe8mA1y0PH_FoAdRHZUxTUlyV24LlfslojIX-9Ld2rhbfzKzJ_lFoFA==>

Tracking The Fine

Facebook has settled with the U.S. Federal Trade Commission over privacy policy violations which misled consumers on what was public and not so public. Adweek's Katy Bachman, "For the next 20 years, the FTC will be looking over the social network's shoulder via third party audits, making sure consumers have control over their personal information. Any violation would be met with a $16,000 fine per violation per day." 20 years! Now that's some good tracking. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj-RcVJUcTYwGikq5TISEoqh1VFv00B5zdkfgxVfLNOnIrx-1qquRkzaMmGKoAVNfCSEJromisNFn6LoB-bZYGKwwCZpNA1tCfP5nbnB9HOKeth1j70rCGSbllfcLkAlc--j_cY9oddZChkhAJKrDZ-GMBuMp63fRUu3V6ckp063bavnov7RstkSyg4Kp5bDGqw=> . 


Visibility For Video

Ever had a video ad start when it's not even visible on the page? That's not a good ad experience! YuMe says it has launched its version of above-the-fold, tracking-like tech that make sure ads get seen but not "heard only." YuMe CEO Jayant Kadambi says in the release, "Ad Visibility technology is not only critical for advertisers to run successful video ad campaigns in which their ads are always visible, it is also necessary to provide advertisers and publishers with accurate brand performance metrics." Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108864315576&s=8442&e=001b3rlhbd-gj_OQcH_ATEzjYTkNFk6KI35VOEgfzY7_aY5i6rA3VuBMeNKi_XQXhj6VMiZtKp4beGn6latKz1LAthdgp1J5wB-7zwc_RQRGwic1ZJaOdxitxRPLyVkkaO9njGuOC7xxbhXpUT_0-Rsyic0PPYiwVEYgn_A6jh3kNSIaECfUK4kHrZ6VNbtVA0fqYEcjIL_pUhyD8aA7_xcOOpRI2Flqrjm4WFGpIgbJPR23Sym9h92j4U1rQDWoID5_1QYJ47ae-g=>

Google-Admeld Approval Imminent 


U.S. Department of Justice scrutiny is almost over for Google's acquisition of Admeld according to All Things D's Peter Kafka. Approval appears imminent, says Kafka, who writes, "It's unclear whether the DOJ will impose any restrictions on the deal. But Web ad players, reading tea leaves and DOJ body language, are betting the sale goes through unhindered." Read the leaves <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIltum1YKnfJrIybMda9d5UFygVfyUaJ_x0jRHd73qzMC7YRM3bVZey8BUshakNORi627sGHr_EUbS_ncC-dgwiy766jk5XCWeVbc6iFmtCZJ5__Yc5jAIh7h81mQypetMNkGWw4FZbeumnK-KryPEG_R4pzVge6KMGunsA41Xc6q0soDJ81BZnLOhYhJ41pshWCFwnBoC6QDcmjAFLn2BpFw59iqlRh9naJ8PgE24W9k8g==> . 


Mulling Yahoo!

The New York Times, among others, reports that the Yahoo! "sweepstakes" may be in the home stretch as offers for 20% of the company were being fielded from private equity firms as well as a consortium which includes Microsoft. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIls5xjCN90itJ32hDM1wbDY0_0Pp6-UeOh4FZI9EOm7WwfK7z84Eudhm0KWhN2nDo59DAX49d_h18PJcaubGyBmV7Gl0U3KOqnIxJUGC35GS8h6_2y0W-_NOeukABFj1oQqz-iHtf7by6y516NmliZYtJr5ftJRpl642pprsL0dTxaJUTULbu4n_FKDCAuvUW5j0WMkE2RwtHy9x_Epn_vBk> . This isn't the end game for Yahoo!. A 20% stake bought by circling opportunists is one thing - but a real strategy going forward is another. The CEO role at Yahoo! awaits its next contestant. 


Needing Ad Validation

On the Ad Ops Insider blog, Ben Kneen shines a light on Adobe's recent announcement around its Ad Validation product and, in general, ad operations' need for a bit of ad tech know-how. Kneen outlines the challenge to-date, "For every piece of creative or ad tag that comes in, publishers have to check the ad against their spec, running down a long checklist, gobbling up hours and hours of time ensuring that the marketer's ad is in line with what the company's predefined limits to protect the user experience on their site. The process is important, but so arduous, that plenty of publishers only check a handful of characteristics, if they have a QA process in place at all." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIlt2B8GU-ROma1FnG_inFUPaZlkFaXu4IaHB6LN4OaaKGDkeBzz9_FKu-SwsIO4g4Vri3mmrb47ukcZezoNgEv86GDtn6rrk1YS-ZZpkb_WLkWKcByRbTe7ou4eAaaAhIr3jpEVRry_nX8PcBI_fZqFyxcxo4YD3hJMTnG-OXi7poKmLR4hJsXImhLYh7u5B4CQ=> . 


The Ad Exchange Problem

Advertising Research Foundation's (ARF) Ted McConnell reviews the ad exchange model on Ad Age. He sees a problem with inventory transparency: "Here we sit, with a miraculous ecosystem that can't quite do what the marketplace needs. Exchanges have no clear way for buyers to bid on inventory quality based on the criteria that mean 'premium.' Would you buy a cantaloupe while wearing a blindfold and gloves? Buy impressions on blind exchanges, and that's exactly what can happen." He wants more data flowing to the buy side. See which data points. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIlvCE_rcjEiE1ZFqS6P4UKEekTRVFAFAEcLJVUB6Tvi44uKubQNmOWtm3pgbTL0qifchBFDmpbL2_biMjqxeXGcPrnr2wLB_SvRrKHFgu7ArCQKgoIvzJVbafi0CNbI2NtC20vA3iNsV3Bi6v71mAyc0OIs0Co4O-qmBAd19K_GWx5rTeUXOQ67lu0e1-yPu2pvgrRzjLjv-z8_c9K-5wxti>  


Mobile-First Not First

Digiday's Jack Marshall explores "mobile-first" publishers and whether they're making any mobile ad dough or not. Marshall cites Pandora's recent earnings report which is showing only "half of its advertising revenues comes from mobile, suggesting it's essentially being propped up by other channels, such as online." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIlt0_xHODpe1RaRgh5RSXf34IzRCY-fqsZoCO1ArfHEdeeG1iZx7YG8cZw0JBsp4tXjTORPj9VfMzx2sBm-gFPFCmkJ7HrOGIHC-5oYA8thTQh6xvufq5y9qabLr4G8jZDQdwcNhftXAbLGUVQ_QbBZneT-CmnLb6ba0k2tczL7nTw==> . Facebook Ad Data Debacle

The Telegraph reports, "The European Commission is planning to stop the way the website 'eavesdrops' on its users to gather information about their political opinions, sexuality, religious beliefs - and even their whereabouts." All of this is in hopes of subverting Facebook's efforts to target users with more effective, while some claim "invasive", advertising. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIltSsDIMEAPD7TPtYezqkcogyIwEvOKA6AHxMRkXCtpKAh1-paFFEbLX1yMY4bPNYLP0lYnnNSLLAP9xcp4h6vHJ80dr3AZTSKZoygrDlDrnjCgMCZzhfV-HTjANJUpSpSIFntCt7ElkZP18DNesKrWkWNn4uwGP4Yt_g1JT8GOTpA==> . It may look like targeting for advertising on Facebook will take a hit. But, Facebook could require its users to accept new, updated terms and conditions that gives permission to use such data - or block the user from the site. What do you think most users will do? 


Display Ads Reincarnated

Andrew Weissman of venture capital firm Union Square Ventures says display advertising is dead in a post on his personal blog. He reasons, "Web display ads are not web native; therefore they do not and will not work." But he's hopeful with what lies ahead saying that it "feels like we are about to enter a new, maybe a golden, age of Internet advertising and monetization." He sees a new world of display ahead - but he doesn't quite put it that way. Read what he does say <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108846397439&s=8442&e=001ISyBQ0OiIluQpN6QPHh934CPUXUC_mwOi6B_SPCYEV3MzCuh_GjoFGb17ZulPjOLB_abWhm2gOpHpZRpGjYoijXI9EhB-dlJuybPlGAxCrds1OLnmNxWTQxshPd47vDJ9feSX69OCsUiIoEV9P1NuCDjnBt69CNbcbdVlEIUUqqEQukAIYmnfA==> .

AdExchanger.com Newsletter
Optimizing The News

For Monday, November 28, 2011

Today From AdExchanger.com...



*	Monday, November 28, News Round-Up <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC67GxveHLZ5OcYp16yEZjPQ2a6sNbY2FH6KbSzJbIHA_6g7CaLlWxh4yOtjRgGFEvkvystfKEUd941Kl-5WV92Ug4t212RVsAGMBoQMm2KAvfhly86zbHZRGMXRa_wvsmnnZpywgtEpccKaxJtZz5-8LApkGYQI2D0c=>  (see below)
*	Yahoo! Begins Requiring Right Media Seats for Demand-Side Platforms' Advertisers <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC64fIYM6sUltrfR2oYagvFuMhbosNRrnMF_l6D7DgRHyscU_Y0DvNunFy96PE5ffEoaxLatoxngyvMCUBIVg_vwEKiPBZZfOyBzXP7dqC_k1OoEKYwDoxc1uM8srjjtOFK5_-yNGj0mG9YGSgf6E7Z6Kj8mnJvz8DLQpkC_Fk74Org==>  "As large direct advertiser relationships are established on the exchange, this will provide Yahoo! visibility into those buyers and their remnant AND direct sales needs. Over time, if it wants, Yahoo! may be able afford dropping CPMs on a direct basis as it has cut out the middleman, which sets up the possibility of larger, bulk buys of direct or remnant inventory on an "upfront" basis by the direct advertiser - a relationship the publisher covets." (visit AdExchanger.com)

DG Becomes Tastier Takeover Target

The stock market has not been a forgiving marketplace as of late. DG can certainly attest to this. The company - which owns ad tech holdings MediaMind, Unicast and Eyewonder among others - is now worth just north of $300 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC66e84J6SKqPFchFCboDoPYdR6ICiEAofc0WsUplQHOmr_OnVDsYRfT4h6iLnurV3q1g0hGYxSQmof9hMESzQ0vytpCVHaAmg8OfHRTEvsnoY2dGY5faN0fOlh4Yv_5UvjljLD5jqGyr77m09d1JUsbMIKJ_kAeFmAs=>  after being worth nearly 3x that 6 months ago. If you recall, MediaMind was acquired by DG for $414 million <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC671Meh7W99T_m_ZSfTqjA0nouJ5JcBWQyv-kYwRbky777QKEYstqteqlxzrm2r0S3VsifycwO1ZRGXAO8FnjL4mvDABIqenbuJbeQv5mTReuesWBFb2TlUN-Y8EPXsT7mPcCfNKy50dkyEJs5sBsAhx7ONOwVgkxBVWPj9WCEUCmw==>  in June. The latest stock decline has been attributed by some to an updated "Underweight" rating on DG stock by a Piper Jaffray analyst <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC65N8_9JHEcGWUFsE7Sam5w-Lw3tuLVaKMXjzmws3K4wObsYmQjKJ_MnwGzcpSJuG4X01JPGUjF5iRB54ZnfTRAbAMM62wDgl-vlkbQVWyFfDL6NHQ7uhfaG14XljZvgCBSNqx8hz-gdAPBEFHygvB4fqtaJrRx61PRbNpZhLc8iW_tqGZ1STMKFyiQPQm0ozoQaKcQL_virbQDTirXCIbTIbyadmP246CuhH8XCLD9EzKTkoHdzhunVHSgVx8OhI0w=>  who sees an aggressive price war breaking out with Extreme Reach run by Fast Channel founder John Roland <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC66W2B3YbYy_ggQmSGktiUhqHUDT570kNS5eih6e61BZpg59lw9c7QcheE3SLYbkUZMF6seu4nVXun6cY5LvKOvfH0GwNWkZ0CxvNRbtjYQy5HzAYMEb_HNfCh-Gq8LtEG4737wrWYXZVQ==> . (Fast Channel merged with DG in 2006.) Publicly, Roland's mantra is very similar to the DG focus as he told Boston Business Journal in October <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC66rR-2NZhNXZi2HI7DMPbk-sdX5Qqf4MONf8N9uueQGb_Z4IQiUyurlgfp7BnUtUh_SYDacPRbAUzNruQGPVNHgCZnu6cBTk3rQzZiqzsAAkpVwNjjgty52688Exp0wtwBt1ox8rzLurOP7bGd6bqcQ0kSUFzUzu2wp44VagV9vCtF5W6-vcfyoG3caYwvrZHu0MlztbZDKbG9MjNVHLDtw> , "What we're trying to do is lead the fusing of two major industries coming together, the TV industry and the online video advertising industry." For now, Extreme Reach appears to be targeting the HD ad delivery business versus the current online ad video market that MediaMind, Unicast and Eyewonder serve. Nevertheless, with DG's budding cross-video-channel platform selling at what might be seen as below market rates, a DG takeover by a company looking to supercharge their video ad efforts seems more plausible than ever before. How about an online ad private company looking to become public in an instant with a little help from some private equity friends? 


Ad Spend Slowdown?

Digital ad spend is slowing in Q4 according to a variety of sources in an Ad Age piece by Jason Del Rey. Macquarie Capital's Ben Schachter tells Del Rey that he has seen Aol and Yahoo! brand advertising take a hit in comparison to 2010. Horizon Media's Donnie Williams says that "his agency has not felt the brunt of this slowdown because of its focus on adding clients rather than increasing budgets with existing accounts." But he still sees sluggishness in CPG and retail. Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC67btuMoHaW8OXHw6VMdeFktEZsPUHs78kLQidPqEOSBXPzh6wpv8qDXAS6jip4mKs4nTylWDCuQiOL9pKc5VxWsaPOZmiTgeMrV8QRCmyZGoRFyV_4N64uYdhV__SY_IrkErTJmfZrqPQvIK8-oaaJp5c_i_s8Q5FMQuxx7ENSVCfkT-36m98JPRsNUJ49vpc2rwyys30UZCQ==>  


Groupon May Darken IPO Door

With certain advertising tech business eyeballing Initial Public Offerings, the recent decline of daily deals supernova Groupon below its IPO price isn't making things easier. The New York Times' Evelyn Ruseli wrote last Wednesday, "The widespread pullback seems to suggest that investors, while eager to capitalize on first-day gains, do not have the confidence, or stomach, to hold on to the Web's latest offerings. That apprehension is likely to be a major concern for high profile start-ups..." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC64ijnV8EhIm6WMLgH31zhAkEnNtJOYmM2nPabOFZAfhwXdR-JKyebmzgEvsjuB2kbLU38lb69Rsbs8bF-7Kzp-Fq2L680TTnYgRKosBffrgmsxTtl58-4i2Zp9oSWCJAQS8GdkO-AiuJse61_iTMJsDjmuFpeScmbhD-nx5ns2-j4QHjGOsiiuZdfwUDUbH2zJPXUeLuIpR-w==> . 


More Yahoo!, DSP Coverage

Last week, All Things D's Peter Kafka followed up his retargeting story <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC662Ru5UG4jUv9IIXqpv15ZLKBOzV4-c_1AwfCjsBI19FH9AOi_1n1eVHmqrm1tly7Gl7B0XPj4mTAkRunbJNUuwZN9faegvtxBMZECFWIfW7W8Ogi3gThaH7D6Z3_KqQQ_0BDhVuMP6tTcEDXReS6G8uiVxZEez4gxQK8trZ5teXV_GnxYzPONX>  with his take on the latest machinations by Yahoo! to require advertisers to buy with their own seats rather than through DSPs on Right Media Exchange. Kafka wrote, "Both decisions are part of a larger strategy designed to give Yahoo more control of inventory it has been selling to outsiders, which is supposed to eventually give Yahoo the ability to sell the ads at higher prices. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC67FFXb9uXcAdqn5CK5YblB18kk57nUUs_LWQ0EgzS-CSbXpon33a_PwdbJDwAkW7OB0VF14Ggtn8PwqsuCHrx8eWARAGk1GH8xhc4FCa9WTycsCpYtQdGX6c-NMMfV460gY0EDBWpYyDtuBOLmIxdsuIwcM7_la63jPx8BHJAhTnms3imAJ3H8WQkfstv_SAtbpSiG-lNqWmw==> . 


Why Ad Ops Rules

In a piece titled "Yield Management Isn't Just for Ad Operations Anymore" on his company's blog, Yieldex CEO Andy Nibley ends up making a good case on why Ad Ops is the center of the storm when it comes to effectively managing yield across all departments of a digital publisher. For example: "The IT group needs to always be one step ahead of a publisher's current technology needs and make decisions to prepare for changes that may arise in the future." IT needs to understand their impact on yield. Rolling Up Video

Ashkan Karbasfrooshan, the prolific CEO of WatchMojo, a video publisher, sees roll-up potential in video except for some popular Gordon Gekko-like attributes. He writes on TechCrunch, "Online video is booming and the are tons of small video companies across production, advertising, distribution, and technology. Yet we have yet to see a serious attempt to roll up the industry. The reasons, I submit, boil down to egos and greed." Read what he thinks should get rolled up <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108795529217&s=8442&e=001x_z5WmEOC66i5H5Fk6ekNS8bakJNtyr8O8pAmJprDKRPpSiEjzEEkyfZ8XTt2UQCIvklVeaOEAzfFQlP1owwmj6OWdbfe5YDSAAcGuIvWfHBeUkltYeGQe1Eys2tZfd8d10amL39iy4NbgGPh-wGB05uqcjRdTjQ> .

May I Scan Your Creative?

Product Manager Drew Bradstock logs in to the DoubleClick Publisher blog and announces "enhanced advertiser-level controls" for publishers. "What does that mean?", you ask... Bradstock says it means DoubleClick scans creative on behalf of the publisher and figures out who the advertiser is behind a display ad (the top 50 advertisers are covered claims Google). The result is that, in addition to blocking capabilities helping to prevent channel conflict, publishers can mine their ad serving data to "see which advertisers are driving the most revenue by geography, domain, channel and a variety of other criteria." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYL6kI0L1mGmriLWooc3SXLhhNCIxsvbFtgCYsJ-2jN_tF4wERK63D-MDUwfWi4I3SOR83Qlhtbcsrqe_VTzk3pk-uGlnQMg426tw8SANlJFZyWxQLkgTABXxTwCfN8yuzLRdqcCsU7ifUHxd3u_R4B1JzeX-VHbTLljE3NtwPaah5UDmbBm0S1pp1wD_0AOrfuzS9pgYoKIMA==> . 


About That Mobile Inventory

Digiday's Jack Marshall writes, "The smartphone ad space could find itself falling into the same trap as online, with direct-response ads traded at rock-bottom CPMs as publisher revenue continues to dwindle." Is the Ipad and tablet form factor the savior for publishers? Maybe, maybe not <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYIxFQzPd7Wt79dLJNvpCuV6P4O2rV3Trad0_UZ9ZqgpFGzmrCJH2BYbTM-N9UTdFbSC9n6X9CRnneaZZWJMlZridb1HRc0_dQIjNT_0YmVherwvuJdRXwHJ0k0VHQCeciSXXUQHm8S6ky679PUTCHUacpXlRFhu6O8IpBucfMqUcA==> . 


Phasing Out The DCO

Ken Nagy says on Zacks.com that former creative optimization (and other stuff) company Adisn has been phased out by its acquirer CrowdGather. But there was a bright side says Nagy, "With Adisn, CrowdGather effectively achieved two objectives: the acquisition of proprietary ad server technology that can create vertically targeted channels for brand advertisers by delivering campaigns across the hundreds of thousands of hosted forums on CrowdGather's forum network; and the speculative addition of a two-person sales force in order to explore Adisn's performance marketing business for a 12 month period." (Adisn was acquired in June 2010 <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYKbG6v2dlSqlJo3okbN78bC9mzS9Xv_9a27aoR_ys6yNz7CmaSWQJBdHoeyDzz0rV1ebNsBauMIn1v-5fjUpWImXlE610SOdy-L-Y7uVTeeuOl87rUAwlhLzArxJ7c1n9WxFMGdZMNsmxvygHpiHOdc> ). Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYLuHw2IuUo6zXo7SegplNtdOV8hxKMhaWYHR3tQLQWcp0hNr5Q3cKSBBaYn69got_iNSkuSSeO2D2f3KNTzdrVKOzh2uDGjIl2XMVlq_mvsRHsSfNlcIjhw3NziM4VtyEmWhyQZOrqs7xMWwkO_5ssT7r5ZjOcJ66uDlhTtknHnFUXDjVYb-_jov8Atcd2G1t8_aoRTNjYT12L65aCagyBP> . 


The $250 Super Cookie

PaidContent's Jeff Roberts covers the settlement Metacafe is undertaking with plaintiffs for their super cookie lawsuit which claims Metacafe was placing cookies that, when deleted by the user, were simply regenerated by Metacafe. According to Roberts, users affected will receive $250 but will will need to "submit a request for reimbursement for any out-of-pocket expenses or costs that they believe they incurred for a reason attributable to Metacafe that could not have been remedied by simply removing any HTTP cookie and/or LSOs associated with Metacafe and using readily available tools to do so." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYLcTwtUgjVpguyul3ju3I80jUMOYdvgxiySnpwBBZla7Uk5QCcUSNECxMHrryMtIevp3hi9cr3LiaNPj65Yic8Uh2dde9x7pgd_WlNPXva9zloH7VOhZygywLMen1BmBtI-n7U6HcyaK_b_0FRDhEAuGbg5QbUhuD605qzVIUUcKBGKUcOiQshNz94ozPsdCoOreoVhgiWq3p-b2G_hSHdT>  


Holding Hands For RTB

In the name of RTB'd inventory, Mobile ad network and publisher aggregator Smaato announced partnerships with mobile DSP providers StrikeAd and Fiksu yesterday. Smaato claims in the release that it is "the largest mobile SSP (Sell Side Platform)" and serves ads in more than 230 countries. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYJiCNLVsrYousgYafx_o-dcy2eT_PfZd2FzLgSppTTukiZrLO59YRnYkTZtaaY_v89vs4MVpcbUHObw6pywqqHBYHFP22AcXJwIOJa5BvH0NNeeOp3QlsGaRvWflE0udkNnLPKWJMf2UBcVgwB2p9jq0oAuQq3N_HL-FclMFtlyxxErd7HnWl9krzR5ZZ8S2d2IcSNBmWAHYQaLl6upwuWDVvZTI3nxKRNXSlfiYp5MOBaQk35Polh4rUJ720e7dwp8jihF5sWy5X4154XHTAjuOPnm_9-MDPgDJ8J4szyuSzcwhR39Mqy-xyNzbLdoLuk=> .

Turning It On

Turn says they are seeing success after it recent entrance into the UK/Europe market with its audience buying and data management capabilities. Mediaweek writes that the company "is on track to make 8%-10% of its global fourth-quarter revenues from the European market." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYJjSDwyzxNG18LjzSkwlaIFXW1Q5LJ33fa9iSuTrUI1il0DwJ5oK9PmDSzXrHE2OSIkbZdxcvtw5WKwbLxdonwjJwxPhkY2Gq-1LAPNCztZtCZPd3P8xsAej5jcbn6zs0YHZNVyxaUB_vQ0wbcFXhA5w8U9scWA9ROP6Vwuf7uHrnqzV8Gq4LO2RVdoUgf7VSmqc29ggK2rmPVj2PM3MqXD> . 


Video Growing The Ad Network

Touting its video capabilities and the ongoing efforts of its BBE video ad network which it acquired last year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYI29ziWwslm-RD9Kk_GgTLiIj8MAqujr4pAF_2ws_4zMsdi0iHxHHg5Gg_zAHx6uGBYHu4tsN8IpImcpNUPDSs5BHya10cwGv6X4a73dXuRz6mT407l_eUxHvxnQfIcIGn8WmcAmUz91u2JBd2aBmQ1Z9RunKxfvY93_ZiyGmTqYq12Z8GSCCeDMxVviNk-OJO1UUKEKhRy-A==> , Specific Media positions itself as a solution for the video ad network future in a press release. The company adds, "Nearly 25 percent of Specific Media's clients now take advantage of the company's ability to run integrated display and video campaigns." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYKhnk3aoG-qtDPFjn1g_gTKVn2OUSb2kBHY2N14hF7YthhQm7iUfmJVfz4A_YmGbwfcuutaP2QgxSjsBEAvDbtXArAmtCIibq0wNHifDvHtrJ0tDhVTwtmsKZwqs8tdRBtUdpdkc_uz8isoSpj09UkzIy78OUjQjpAN-G62k1Dh4EU8DhwdZjhBYXdhfQQAk3uKe0W6tah7e2T-u3hOP_VVBYbTqw7Pl7E=> . 


Big Data... Boom!

The Atlantic gets in the act with its own brief feature piece on the big data explosion. It's not all about ads (what's wrong with them!). It's about R&D, too, as the authors explain, "Customers are acting as unwitting business consultants for these companies. Our purchases, searches, and online activities are being tracked to improve everything from websites to delivery routes and drug manufacturing." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108737016811&s=8442&e=001LFp2SKA4pYKnwoWLy8s_bxhfOhTwyhdXgaKNK8FoZguVtNhJ-wt5shzNLT6Ow0PPpp-8bT-YbqhvIFtVHlFMu-b7L5M7Wan9hsS2Yb6Q5ai5Ms2mAocyr16GfbCTK86xsGJlgPRhj2CPVhTiPsUgIYYMTrU8AwZr7edkJY-_sfeYOY8zARP2QJS2277L8-CLKe-XalX1UYKl5lU7N_rQ_8gwuW9kTs3W2FqZdiPHzbiIZNdAJiRxhw==> .

Ebay Looking For Recommendations

In an effort to apparently maximize yield for its digital shelf space, Ebay is buying Chris Dixon's Hunch - or so says indefatigable blogger Mike Arrington who estimates the prices at around $80 million and adds, "The Hunch recommendation technology will be used by Ebay to revamp their own ecommerce recommendations. Dixon will take over Ebay's existing 50 person recommendations team, and start a new office in New York." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS19G0UG7YVL9Mqy2HX106Ww8ek8co6x7oKVlZDHFsaHCYIIg2JVKELuntPmtGITzhxIBNfyn6Yr0Y8n82Nl93gj_Qug1kOmwhWIE1JqUMJ_UtMrunsZgQCeqBLh7ya-mMc3LiyZUsWPkenyTWKmcjcacEPvrs_ZMFGQcNGad3Bue1pUUhl-CZVV> . Improving the recommender - it's the yield optimizer for Ecommerce. Ebay hopes it bought a good one. 


The Mobile Ad Audience

Jumptap revealed some stats from its mobile ad network showing that the mobile audience can be a fickle bunch. From the release, "Samsung smartphone users access applications 27 percent more than iPhone users. On the flip side, iPhone users are twice as active on the mobile web as Samsung smartphone users." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS1XfQAQGPXlp1aNihWleKwlKCKQ0XNrx_3LvqcRwO64qDpEhf7vL1qHEN_pIlztU1eZl51Tbx75YFKi95alTyi8NpKZXccpRzGY_23PUoeQ6v7wLuyEt0aW8yW6weYcvuO-C0a4Zuta9fugR2Ss0kkJrsR8KnTICON2nmCNnBLx748wLT24-y546N2pgSKjtt9TznJywhwXsA4RQVf7m-7H1Y2KGAZPieI=> . Gaming apps appeal to the younger crowd on Samsung says Jumptap, and news and entertainment rules with older audience on the iPhone. The more appealing demographic is... it depends what you're targeting. 


Subscribing To Digital Ads

Venerable magazine The Atlantic says that, in October, for the first time its digital revenues have overtaken its traditional, magazine revenues. The New York Times' Jeremy Peters writes, "The Atlantic, which expects to make about $18.6 million from advertising this year, or slightly more than half of its total revenue, said the growth in its online share of business was not because of a decline in the share of print revenue." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS0kpm-dZjYQDjHPPM4jEzaeFc9ojQTSdXqFgn-HqyzKaE0vsKHCdN6Gz9jIyI-1XJA190daI2HUvKWKgbzZWk7PEnptHlCgfN7fSFFoaxsP_YCf2E-q1JdaKX3LsisnM4RsikldFRyjWRfNvxGhiJV__tNqzp-H77W5xr0XUGI9qbr95LKx6Ao0>  


Right Video, Right Audience

Max Knight of full-service media buying and data management platform Turn reviews what it takes to make video campaigns work online. No surprise here as Knight pours from a pitcher of data-driven Kool-aid, "Audience targeting capabilities. This is important in display and no less so with video. Marketers need to be able to reach the people they want and to control the frequency with which their targets are reached." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS2bN9CU2yGxBq9Oi9NUFzeiola9Xk2JctnNAXKiazgV-bdmXefeSzT5Gm6DvsctyhnZVpaUmjQ-sxYCqq7r7YayUHlx89qJefJRX3dR9OhwtTDB0vGLflo4JXEg-vEEPyme_d9IxyZUksCJwKZfemTysh02GJoSVj8=> . 


Relationships Vs Tech

Speaking like your favorite "premium" publisher, Apple Store builder Ron Johnson says in the Harvard Business Review, "People come to the Apple Store for the experience - and they're willing to pay a premium for that." Think about it online - is your store an experience or just another clunky ecommerce site? Johnson says that success starts with people: "The staff isn't focused on selling stuff, it's focused on building relationships and trying to make people's lives better." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS02uWijI4e_zjjYSl0xVyjNfUl0zz2XKfjk62jSpIN632jg8zuCG88jtAjiHoBOe1ac99PoPcOeOeIXvMex_tDLgALoaYa4b-hxY-h-ahoRH17z51J9LtCx2827SzQqz84YJBF_TdhuoHzAF1gIWGl2lavN0JE-bvT2qwhq19t8nQ==> .

Creating The Right Mix

On the comScore Voice blog, Frank Reding discusses the intricacies of Marketing Mix Modeling (MMM). He admits, "One criticism of MMM is that because its insights aren't available until after an advertising campaign has run, they are not actionable." He ultimately agrees and says that creative is the big wild card in marketing mix modeling. Redick champions pre-testing creative. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS0tye1vtV7SAjgwKa4Jud4gHo6pNwPvUvOBItdHxLj3OHAnZ03GjwMbfsnbCnRF2GMTydACYZW-wfOHGLSHg_afJFzBLdm2EXnfZhBSbJK8icrNwUuF0nr3PNum1Hu3jlqjQTt_7vV6Bfd7iO1lTNqAl1z5etTslDmdSorWFMfHkQ==> . 


Do-Not-Tracking It

In this past Sunday's New York Times, the publishing company's editorial team urges lawmakers to adopt a Do-Not-Track law and "act on the F.T.C.'s recommendation to establish a system that would allow consumers to effectively opt out of all tracking of their online activities." Read "A Push For Online Privacy. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS3XSJnfdNUj55UtLqxKYPmBmHM_1XTEsBNFpOpZW3XmSgi87o-MmN5sjdZ6GTI-EzF2-1PBUuv3Ckp9rS2OIFua2w9NJ_48yBFoIddRyyNZ7GLLqc9ZGVNdw7vT2LhVkm2lS5PklQOZRY_cHnR_v6Z1JxcOGGYeqKL2jgFf1YnPL3Gyn2YnG7EIh_Wr5EqngLs=> " On his Buzz Machine blog, Jeff Jarvis responds - Balderdash!. Actually, he writes, "I do not object to any of these tracking behaviors. They are, in my opinion, necessary to pay for the content we get from The Times and The Journal and much of the rest of media. They are used to reduce noise, repetition, and irrelevant advertising and content." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108720024481&s=8442&e=001DBksjtQHnS0aPgaR8yjKAjGHdPhb4BJp7vqZcEybLrkah4uChm4eKgEgGSGnwwewRtVzti87zAFhdCnQxX9Gh_xrGVjsyms76YTSE0iODGPyNdaukf5IJXXrqg-j4DbDZY4xnIcBXgHhEI5BiadQxfX4OSlXJH-w>

Facebook Ad Metrics

Rob Hof provides an in-depth article on Facebook advertising in the December 5 issue of Forbes. Display ad success metrics, the click and other industry analytics pain points make an appearance as Hof writes that Facebook is trying to find a better way but it's tough, "Even Facebook concedes as much. Closing Facebook's Ad Week presentation with [Facebook ad exec David] Fischer, Mark D'Arcy, a former Time Warner ad exec who's now Facebook's director of global creative solutions, said of Facebook ads, 'We're sort of like 1951 television.'" Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mNDWlFcBFI1-_qtakLKUeWiTPj7H-zWi9wIijZ64QKs-taMmpaf3QSEukqOQZReMQ8Ko4ia1luk_U1b3b2VNCbTg4OJgmjhwmX-E58OZDod6oCQoiBsM35EtmIEYeGYJagGpy7KqW6fu4lyZ7ZUx9JKrYZI7TvNU4x2_vjRgfNLhhgRSP1E2fhkC_WBG2b2zUtOhfhA9c0UBQ==> . Will Facebook build in-house or will they acquire solutions and talent? Big brand marketers want more. 


SOPA To Clean House?

Digiday's Jack Marshall covers the latest acronym to set the wider digital ecosystem ablaze, SOPA (Stop Online Piracy Act). Marshall writes, "SOPA proposes the U.S. government should be given the power to shut down or 'blacklist; websites that violate copyright laws." And that means ad networks, search engines, and ISPs would have to cut off services to offenders says Marshall who presents the risks for all sides - including publishers. Read the coverage. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mPnsxRHsy7beaQxx5e7WQB-8zdLrxDi6TWiWfkDZkObqd4Qvb-JoN8JoAQRd-DK7jgyW50xnxpoyo7MoFsYzhPFMxd6539HKhkzfGvkcN_1xgPmrVCLyKzC3NdFgMf8eXUNXkEJFnJ7evgbm-uFVX_-78flWXUEyssWHp2O8Ac5sIBTTXagTXcp>  


Collegiate Incubators

U.S. universities on the east coast are trying to catch up with their west coast brethren, as Harvard is the latest to open up a startup/incubation lab. Pass the digital test tube as this lab - called i-lab (like Skylab <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mPoJ0mbh9piRy7W4ybFEMhLsoXO8EQgKL4UV60Yy2I1Usf3vqQfNIbNzVqmv_YTx4anLYPJqQyXYTbuwDDdhCTdN2M_oQKTqP_WSGvPhAiXXrRmM9LUdKb5> !) - has the latest and greatest doodads. The Boston Globe reports, "Last week, Mark Zuckerberg, the cofounder of Facebook, dropped by to check out the building and get a preview of a company being developed there that will stream live TV over the Internet. He dubbed it 'actually pretty cool.'" Read the coolness <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mPDjfA6XBe11D6kGnmm696cCuDz8PdRQmeHJhwvLGLNeWZvnzOQ4q8NF0raD06iniI04KRj_4do32yfIQ-3MfaaVaCoEJvMPbg8ohGPAbeM7BErXb8TV0GOF8qeFrspojArQX08O8wMDPdQ1O7TTDN_DBwqVpYoGbi3_ga7Zd7MNAF2v_zzAZ9lv520gzqdcvaigOAv_EhLJQgXYeASSlZKziPlev6_66v74KmQWkrYMVMc4sS8aIYih_A8tzSF1tY=> . 


Local Run Rate

On TechCrunch, Yext CEO Howard Lerman shares the latest success his company is seeing for local listings "plumbing" on sites like Yelp etal. TechCrunch reports the local data synchronizer's "PowerListings business is on a $12 million revenue run-rate, and Lerman expects it to surpass his pay-per-call business by the middle of next year He hints that more local listings partners will be added to the service in December." Lead gen-ners love the listings. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mPy_6VlzQvYTSNZQnBWfUvdCDSIjaL_FQBRisU2lDIppLWcGG8KEk5kE9W15s3PYT0h_rNWr1FoD6AOKjL5Ca16Fh7vmJ1pV9IyTLJ_Qp4jHb9lxJJ1XAcPMuFj78zTZ3uzUNUeiWn3CbPzZR-InpknmTSpCqp7Tuw=> . 


Ad Exchange In China

According to Adaline Lau of ClickZ Asia, Google's DoubleClick Ad Exchange was the talk of a recent Shanghai ad event and a Google DoubleClick exec "has been making the rounds with media agency professionals in the Greater China region to talk about its AdX and demand-side platform Invite Media." Is your company in China? Is your agency? How many fingers am I holding up right now? Retargeting In-Store

Amazon and others are banking on the fact cost-conscious consumers will want to comparison shop when they visit stores this coming holiday season and "Black Friday" (the day after the U.S. Thanksgiving holiday). That's why they've provided a little self-retargeting device (my words) - a mobile app for their smartphone which takes in-store product prices and then compares it to what Amazon has to offer, for example. App as useful ad. Read more in the NYT <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mOWBtLxeT4Ya_BL0kYKcIG-MO_1sslUE4GqJiFHvQAbJLAxI5ZqnxKqO-BTEPuKzFEQu_yXBmw_tn0x9PmlPnFUqschqe-Fgn9hsCdyq4Xzk34q_D5oWlzqwu05uRCDmbSZwizN3euGHYnnb0-jinPasr-m4VXkk-W0KbLj-I2y_PlWOsEnbgzrYAQBuBryQnO8wcjsPX9vK36pSdo_5W1uKzdm_-lsv0c=> . 


Targeting Digital Radio

Prepping for 2012, online radio service provider Pandora has productized its targetable, U.S. demographic data for politicos as the company announced its new product for local and national ad campaigns. From the release, "Campaigns of all sizes are able to deliver their messages to custom voter zones in an uncluttered radio environment, because on Pandora only one audio advertisement plays per break." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mNldkxxHhJ9TcETF_XhDZxj4LHJjE-Ucef3_pFj5tbB-a4CT-LNLgNdyJlcqSs1I382gpJHb1gNYKcii6jHHVgDDiFNMAMjKAo9S9LG0aRr7i1PzZwBnz3Znbhx_OP7ufCf-bqKGoEVCV_iVrzT0NS_YkvYLbEHXJ3kdDtlTFk3_g==> . Tying retargeting of those users to other channels (video, display and mobile) will be something DSP-like companies will tout as the 2012 U.S. election season approaches. 


Projecting Ad Revenue

Consultant David Sonn gives his basic how-to on projecting online ad revenue. After the first year with ad networks, Sonn says, "When projecting revenue over Years Two through Four, increase your $1.20 per 1,000 page views first to an average of $3 CPM, then ultimately to a maximum average of $10 CPM. These are general guidelines and it's best to be conservative." Read how Sonn thinks you get to $10 here. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108665451924&s=8442&e=001qHm27vuC8mMbKDPbs6BQj9rfDY7thHRZvwLZCLkjR56dgnZtW5d-H7MjbKqItDGaOW7OgcRrZ-Jd81S-y8Kpd4HY3aBejwVzv0yymVuIs-Ju6vkNbI3ri6l8cInh8lI_ofSxSKtmtQ978EnJIAE4d-eP3gs9b7QG-SvMiOMLgafMFHu164j4n1aM3WOcTXJ9d9DApQwq97c=>

24/7 RTB

24/7 announced that its Open AdStream ad platform is now real-time bidding(RTB)-enabled. The company claims that differentiation from other SSPs and ad exchanges includes "a single decision engine" and "instead of integrations between multiple systems, the experience for the users viewing the ads is improved due to faster page loading speeds and there are far less complexities for publishers managing their inventory." Among others, 24/7 is working with its WPP partners The MIG and Xaxis on the demand-side. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zauKvF-VrCXomNB8bJLIV2Y252Gi1X5J5SNEN78TxHGQ5h7-LfpP4Vm8aeyTKvrL601aWgL6HOTLpF4F1IhBW4CYQFM--_eoTktZUzF5uT8G89qTZWo2Ms-FUbtEaF2K2EE44WDO6-gL4tOavQyxothn2hQqqBeqwcDA0v47FxOtwZLuA63GzbTDnZABAf6QZ8KvJVBhS5wZU0da0fNq4fB1q4slQ-UWvexTUZkI8QU1g==> . Ad network becoming exchange? 


Sharing Data With Planners

Have your own data? Consider creating a standard -or index. Sharing data company ShareThis launched its Social Quality Index, which it calls "the first measure of Web-wide sharing activity and will provide publishers and advertisers with site rankings across 27 key content categories." The company said agency Starcom MediaVest Group is using to help it with their media planning. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zb1zHYMU5CDGi1GUeNJPqBjz36HQK5g-g5p4JSvTlhHealJy-LjnhVdDTJxt85aG--85Mxj3rGruLLKMSU_v0QMg39NJ5FUP2TwQhXfNqf8oUPUEYI5wmIFRDoFNrazgB5YnPYFXlFTsQrixqiIAG9WFeW4E09lm-uzAMUvLMRYBJEtWlogd2e6tqNSwjjQrqhndFyImzuPg5YwOKoFxPtkhquc4cSGHme-RWveNs5rtpieE0e_sgq7> . 


Publishing And The Ipad

Publisher firebrand David Koretz falls on his sword on MediaPost as he admits he thought he had publishing on the Ipad figured out in an article hearlier in the year. But after watching a GQ app whither on his Ipad desktop (Ipadtop?), he decided he was wrong and it's time for GQ to add more features. The Ipad audience is needy. Ideas for GQ and others include publishing to the Ipad before publishing in the printed magazine. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zakNcPqNqlcml0w9I815v9Qzj6paqDnKF__0lDhKCneWfTNzIetfS0Y6gZrwgOzN9Rv_MFY_BPVzNgrX3An2NtiKBTx_Ub8O3LjrPgvba9de45rss9p8gQqJdJQAaRMl2OkyyzDmIViofTOvlEbwEsVytH4-_zpvQcOmIpn5kGwBCLVGVLamnHklfI_b1tFXJY=> . 


RTB Attributes

Madhu Vudali, product maven at ad network Brand.net, picks up with Part II of his thoughts on why the comScore ad network rankings may lack relevance considering the advent of the Real-Time Bidding age (RTBA!). Appealing to the agency client, he offers tips on how to pick a buying platform. He thinks the partner needs a bidder that it owns: "Having a bidder gives the media partner control over scale (potential inventory and unique reach) and operational efficiencies. It is also an indicator of their level of technical investment and sophistication." Read all the tips <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zZEQ9VYtiCQUAfYV7FWfTeLtkuo4V4Ss1lAaPkzxzQtSE2ZG7LOfTwbut6SI99hLd2-cVNkFQ3ojXLB3T_-1YCeGYgciQHV3AR1aae456JkE7sVWRKX-RXOgyrwjDJG66RO7A8mrc5rynid32-wp9Le-tBzge0pix39XOlyt3C10XqT1i3xExIX> . Ad networks and agency trading desks are at the beginning of a slugfest as ad networks try to leverage their tech ownership with clients versus agency trading desks who prefer to license software and platforms. 


Guaranteeing Display

CEO Nick Pahade shares his views on the industry and innovations at his digital media workflow platform company, TRAFFIQ. He says, "We built a budget allocation engine that we're currently piloting with 10 different agencies that we think is a different approach to how guaranteed display on TV is currently happening." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zbRLkZMaam8j9m806bjoAaywySvMBEmjHKHPN9doAaIhMfTapZjfkN7Y0KJwJSkvw9oweBK_0vBOzK7JsAe3GpDAW85ZMChUilxcdjn75U8phbOWS4quEsppAviXx2-8ArWLOV_smxHkkRN7bMP9-oPDxb0qD6eM0rqQEtnamKHJ1SLON7NF2_flemcXsGaOGU=> .

Dealing With Groupon

In a deal that's being positioned as "newspapers fight back against Groupon," many of the biggest publishers announced a joint venture called Travidia that is focused on ecommerce intended "to help advertisers reach consumers making purchasing decisions." Publishers are trying to get ecommerce into their platforms to unleash another revenue stream. Read the release. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zY3Xgs5ZH7d7GMyK9brSeJYCc_ceX-Imbn3doi7CdrGlJewEVnoj2RoBK1KE5YiytQdeQDYH6H85-shJrI-00rMLRwK4UrJPxoTZBJxkvD1bzOtekDGkqnZuGP4mPjGgP5WHYn6bXnGmSbSffEjuE8VIWjblTnIhplRoZJf_GZLX5zDp8oxCwFuHRcQDR081QOKkJKbqGjmPuPRYqxR7uVxfj0rpDLgwQ5lLscwf6wLCvJjZXAJRD5w>  And if publishers want commerce to succeed, they may want to make sure they have mobile covered if new ecommerce research results are to be believed. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zYvp4IMrR1YQGB9mqWRaLJCxdeFcPC7pO7ZyNfGsvPNT682pLYtOjoSmlUakLb9rGUx7EZNowpCybzRTBqINykb929MtX1JGViJE5f8VsJtWMv4-jMlnIrjurkvWt8TztOJed5BNJYu0Iq_2zf-1UDykOsKIAPycOM=> . 


FTC To NAI 

If you can't beat them, get one of them to join you. Or something like that. Marc Groman, the chief privacy officer of the Federal Trade Commission, is joining the self-regulatory ad network group Network Advertising Initiative (NAI) as its next executive director and general counsel. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zb9mdIkwHb_aG3UntPJXyQBSh_zOqtJccovhUWEczwrzEKihb51f7iFE3JWbhuUBSfat-Ix9TQN3g6ZTSeITcWqRZ6luH0ooK-uOYDlyIz0qhbIhu-p3ZP5E5wT8kJRCKzZJkmArhyNDCmdbJqafqwzXUi0rkqkBWwB6n3J8dubi5ZuW90IHZT5kX-zDkv3O4piiXqF_aipITLy4b3OgDcf98D7RMtMXY4bGgINnkq9rAwZdSsrzO4oZK3SEi-6HSGe5zmYSpj3sA==> . 


The Seller Life

Doug Weaver lives up to his surname and reveals the choices sellers must make as they grow their careers - do they live on the Mountain? Or the Rain Forest? Cue the wild call of the monkey... Weaver writes, "The Mountain is not as crowded as the Rain Forest, and those who live there are able to live quite well... given the proper tools, preparation and provisions. While those in the Rain Forest busy themselves managing commodity, those on the Mountain work to create new value through ideas, connections, synthesis and vision." Or both? Make it rain, Mountain Man <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zbMA4Zr0YufVzIlJCW_ZEXxs7bsNzlvwwc7pMrlTMSwSGaG1lgayeYwuR4w94WpMS0v8EffOhfDrUVKE1sobcCHCpJbjGLFQs0fyRWg2a51AIet2MgnJJcGOG7x7TchvtGqsEBBOCiVLdbDnzIel05d> . 


Spend Slowing, Digital Strong

Bloomberg reports on a recent presentation by Publicis CEO Maurice Levy who said at a recent investment conference that his company "has let business units freeze hiring to avert layoffs and has seen a 'leakage' of spending from worried clients." Nevertheless, he said digital growth remains a bright spot. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zY-49eaZ2_U8bnuRXLt9-Y7U6TTG1v9H8U5wWP1KQ2rI3dbLtBzimvlsEdj9qoZBuCeAZjaHbMPqOnn4EsHoPxhsJs5NqkWed92296A2fwZKsnenIyqQd0aIPfvAOYw-vpITx72fDypEdrf0tGIdcwfdniaWwU2IkZz8fS8ngmrT8doQK7GTdwtdb1FBjVUnE9FTR5DVGG0G_aZmsgWBtEXDVcjPetFW6U=> . 


On Mobile Fragmentation

Ad Ops Insider scribe Ben Kneen continues his musings on AdZerk's Run of Network blog with a piece on "Mobile Fragmentation." Channel and device fragmentation make the list here as Kneen writes, "From the small feature phone screen to the massive iPad screen, the range of mobile is immense. Even on a single device like the iPhone, certain versions support higher quality creative than others - think the enhanced 'retina' display on iPhones 4 and higher." Pick up the pieces here <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108651607179&s=8442&e=001JBC1QpQr_zaWTJi0CY8EwnkkjB8Xk8yPQ7NCVwrJQ8J9UOA4wWs-QZ59uFAYC1uAnw9Wyff3f7oxk8_TcntXB_wHA9tnDys1S4wHf1UueEtpE2gfYieYnpm8EDYu-rCTV_fsHnJZcIfh0gf-Uwt_BAgfIH4WmdCXWQnI-sBAm7I=> .

Getting Strategic With Video

YuMe has received a cool, strategic $12 million investment from a group that includes Samsung Ventures among others as YuMe appears to be clearly warming to the role of solutions provider for the connected TV future - in addition to its PC-based, online ad network capabilties. Read the release <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLoWl55Qr5sJhKO_FLEASpPOU3fM-mBJazfzmNYa0-6xyw9L9SAkoLt5TUi6i2XYGRmIVrJBUmEwGCxbokHdQysfy3QJaUuk32O4zErV8hVV3P9or0C00_YyVm2LXshd9iD9F0auJPglJZws2wRtH1doZjeatRa3-uOqpPrbIEuHfzZ7-B6vcitMXiOc4dgu6ysa4btRwjLT9x95LIJOoElEuz-A-pLYbQE=> . It's an interesting conundrum for video ad networks - you don't want to be positioning too early to the connected TV party. And of course you don't want to be too late. For example, in discussing a what you might call a subset of connected TV - addressable TV - TidalTV's Scott Ferber told AdExchanger.com earlier this year <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLrxLKh6yOF0JfjUC6A9H9rnLfHHMctq1A7fCti0mWNyVvlT0h5yVS4d3bjCxhV86-UD0tQeWWqGk69HS_TQowCZmICD8LAAYU-szATpzQSinJDDK1mXICDWyNDznAEIgIoDxaazrIQcBA==> , "Strangely enough, we built our capabilities for [addressable TV] first. So, actually, in a weird way, it's the greatest application of our technology, the addressable television. It's the least volume part of our business. How's that for an ironic statement?" Part of what's driving this move to connected TV appears to be device manufacturers getting in the game such as LG which announced a partnership with YuMe a couple of weeks ago (TVexchanger.com Q <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLqXrONIuLuoHCjL0tfcWmDCJMVR9mjTJDja4oFMWLhcaR7-CDO_G2lH2HWrw-CNgIuFypKUcuvG7p6cd8tdGPKB96ys2htJgTqiPA6IExvoydtXltjVJ5dbecY41l6Dx3Dlh-a9nHx2zw==> &A) and, of course, YuMe's new strategic Samsung among others. 


Garlinghouse To Exit

The Business Insider reports that Brad Garlinghouse will be leaving Aol where he has been "President of the Applications and Commerce Group and head of AOL's Silicon Valley operations." Sources tell TBI that Garlinghouse "was frustrated that AOL has been reduced to playing defense and is not paying attention to some of the great product work his team was doing out on the West Coast, particularly its mobile products." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLqXrONIuLuoHL9B2dUrotYSuRnS17p82Sr9YOZnPavsquSqgv0qOu_zRL9NtAGgh2si_b5GvXCnFR4HC1PVv9rjcwaEbV-lvqc3Qk92TVkdWFAx5QBQ8kZpVTG8YyH4u0-_17Q9UVI5Ka29u8XmITbOEM15xJRYoebXODuq1uM9SA==> . If true, it's not the first time Garlinghouse has been frustrated with management. He wrote the 2006 classic email "The Peanut Butter Manifesto" while at Yahoo!. Read about the good ole days <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLostLfy3jDK462_wdSKtyboyjyKwVAG9O7BA-k9O3XquY5z_wPWiCwBzqOZ8Y4Dzq55Sqj4CyT8897-QQUdZmxJGk1I4DjT1xDHKm-05P0Yw6RY-TNJ6lwH0pq-VJsB8KvmtdJAnlAvg3YWx_4wP-yScAce33t53HB-oszVNFdaQsDCrVZt94_Wny3dBwLbXrw=> .

Discovery Intent

On the Yieldbot blog, Jonathan Mendez takes issue with comments in a Wired article involving Twitter's Jack Dorsey where Dorsey suggested that, among other things, following users through Twitter is equivalent to showing intent. Mendez instead sees Twitter's strength in what he calls "discovery intent" and explains, "Discovering more about what you're interested in has always been Twitter's greatest strength. It leverages both user-defined inputs and the rich content streams where context and realtime matching can occur. Just like Search." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLq1b3Ahf0ju24J5KP3uvYrymE8sm-4dXrxItw68j1HLeo4qhAbhoJXLNRkW9BpTQLyfbyVjEbs5AyBgvyo_k1Hminfj0gFHUQMa5oMuY_Ae5478rTTHVU8I> . 


Video Uniques

Nielsen says that video minutes viewed online are still increasing rapidly but the number of viewers aren't. Why? Nielsen's Joe Holz explains, "The greater increase in time spent viewing compared to the number of unique viewers is likely due to an increase in the amount of video content available for viewers to watch, especially long-form content like movies and TV shows on sites like Netflix and Hulu." See the pretty graphs. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108634839021&s=8442&e=001Y2Qgbz9BVLqnwNDzh6h7SwbcvkVx_huExJMwSKVCPbgtg-RpL0qyAsTHDXKNKZETorf_qjJ5uZz9JBvfwjOlpocqb4U85owYSYnIqhtbUeMWsTy9FzWcJ3fzJKGdpRGBzXabsEmFqVT4hTxPXMeKFWFMDkCmb_ZWalrnUSTUR_quslmT6AKOG1Wkybr0P1mpTzDULITQqlTWpHmmULyZvgKVEZCcJRFu>

Tracking Exchanges

As part of its Digital Strategy Supplement, UK-based trade mag Marketing Week looks at, well, digital strategy including one of the most popular opinion piece subjects of all time - the last click - which leads to a discussion of attribution -which lead to French Connection digital marketer Jennifer Roebuck saying, "Large companies with massive budgets are probably leveraging their attribution model for ad exchanges, but most retailers in our space are just starting out with it." It's still early days. Privacy Icon For Websites

BrightTag is getting in the icon/privacy business as it has a solution which enables a web publisher's visitors to control their ad network settings on a publisher's site. On The New York Times' Media Decoder blog, Tanzina Vega quotes CEO Mike Sands who says that his "company considers its new privacy button feature as 'a layer that sits below and has connectivity to' the Digital Advertising Alliance's icon-based program.'" Look At You, Mobile Ad Server

Mojiva has received a coveted seal of approval from Microsoft Advertising. Microsoft Ads' Kashif Ali explains that his company "will integrate Mojiva's Mocean Mobile platform into our existing suite of digital advertising technologies--such as AdExpert, pubCenter and adCenter--to serve mobile display ads across our global network of mobile apps and websites (...) In addition, the Mojiva network will integrate into the Microsoft Advertising Exchange for Mobile, bringing additional demand into the system by the first half of 2012." Amazon Or IPO

The Business Insider drank from the rumor cauldron (or something like that) yesterday and said that Amazon may want to acquire sell-side platform PubMatic. TBI's Nicholas Carlson quotes a source and writes, "This source said a Pubmatic executive and another plugged-in industry executive told him that Pubmatic recently fielded a $300 million takeout offer from Amazon, but turned it down in favor of going for an IPO." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108622232980&s=8442&e=001v5qrzG-gqeGTnN_P_xTfrrZWSWDuedoj1vOKshb2v5Qfjmkn2TVuJ7USfD9d1AQkL4WngJ6j36F2H58qxJbu3IgfJ4k-Mh56J1pZk8ggzkxzh89IHxkfuPq-buTdhj9FrDsxUM-tWYpguawf9ZDgADm0seGnRGrXAMR2FUppriWGG9LbHasVAJf9G6rfqw5LGZ0nG3lvqzfPC4T5nEgYV54xiubZ4Jo_pjtbtbNOcQ0=> . 


More VC Dollars For Video

Video ad network BrightRoll, owners of the BrightRoll video ad exchange, announced that it has taken a new round of funding to the tune of $30 million and led by Trident Capital. The company reports that it has continued to double revenue year-over-year and "currently manages 2.25 billion video ads per month, or nearly 1 out of every 3 U.S. video ads served, according to data from comScore and BrightRoll internal reporting." Conde Nast Goes Exchanging

AdMeld may be temporarily caught behind a Department of Justice curtain as it awaits approval for Google buying the sell-side tech company, but that hasn't stopped it from closing more private exchange deals including Conde Nast. Conde Nast tells Ad Age that if you want to buy on its Ad Meld-supplied private exchange, "The minimum requirement for advertisers to get access to the exchange was that their fourth-quarter ad spend with Conde Nast this year had to be higher than last year's." Acquiring For Mobile

Mobile marketing ad tech company Velti remains acquisitive as the owner of Mobclix has now bought Mobile Interactive Group ( <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108622232980&s=8442&e=001v5qrzG-gqeGs24UCCr-pLFw_-v7HY3b75rJ_zN6fHqHIrcTyPqsLsysCHMMDh1fc701TvX7dcwbZfyVwYpikqNkcwe5uMK3T4i-JGKyj_-TmsEtCv7lJww==> "MIG") for $25 million with various incentives and earn outs thereafter. From the release, the company claims, "This acquisition makes Velti the world's largest mobile marketing company based on revenue, customers, and technology holdings." To back it up, the company offers only that MIG had "$100 million in gross billings, more than $20 million in net revenues in 2010..." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108622232980&s=8442&e=001v5qrzG-gqeGnj0rkEzmOD9TCZkkROjRkyHNslkdiB-pWGEScwL9zCP6Y8scfdPkpzzWI0HrFX5HSkHJHszX6WlAFz_tTPernPHU2pUZuO1YtYNh2M_szoKsUN2hfl0gdU3yVCuK_A4dZjuZw9VCSCJRWPvk_5ZqjKKVe4A2amzU=> . 


The Scarcity Of Scale

David Pakman, venture capital partner at Venrock, says scale is becoming scarce in the startup world. As a result, he writes, "We are entering a period where the business model innovation will become more important than the innovation producing traction and engagement. It has always been impressive to see startups with incredible traction. But just using this traction to produce scale will not be enough to create the great companies of tomorrow." It's The Algo

Google just announced "ten recent alogrithm" changes to its search algo. Among the changes according to Google's Inside Search blog, "Fresher, more recent results: (...) we've made a significant improvement to how we rank fresh content. This change impacts roughly 35 percent of total searches (around 6-10% of search results to a noticeable degree) and better determines the appropriate level of freshness for a given query." Make mine "real-time"! Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108622232980&s=8442&e=001v5qrzG-gqeGvhk5MZnVsf_wwgCNExlI6Itj3vm1oby-90QacFmp0mhMZzw6T_uNPQAvv3au3UdTPjfrl_Sv6JlQ2wQ96t1KQanDPMqOxDLnOoo72GbV9v-qiN50TY-L9AMQnTOJ2uIPt3B5ES-rBVT7yQRiKc8MmgFw6TIetr_LfP9EnzbFPbYfdPXJyIQ2J> .

Video Is H-O-T

Hot hot hot <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraeemO4pJ7vwnMtoyVnHzhkOkmYUlqNsrOXn76gcEC1ac2AdYRnL59Oz5DHWLue-DjnjiUMdER50xHtMuOcwKvPRxIO1AtAa57CDDJe_rZng04onS43W1SoX0G3Ona_-vMg5MWXBS6zsKlw==> ... Video DSP and analytics firm TubeMogul says pre-roll is "catching up" with online display ads in terms of inventory with real-time bidding attributes. See the graphic <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraee7RZLN-b0pGTOemR7kWrjxf6zqWkYQ70FcJpAfZGma67fF7N5GT4yLN-L_O4zgQeAk4ZladMdfSLq5PvY4MGJ_7yxlZEiBdIvyyk7OT94YOgLOwRfVFibbAsW6-C-t13xN9I8OsOrzeYQXGowOg0xu-pEewUvIche0_7HVSlBKii6Zl3WKFqdgcC0lgVGllyRSUVKa8fGiiSQUux17_HWqDjRVjUzNgbjAgWVPE_HEwvWN7cGQdnOl3G8zvrVEvjw=> . According to a company blog post, "In the past five months, pre-roll volume grew by an average of 34.9% per month, far outpacing display advertising's 7.8% monthly growth rate. In November, we are seeing an average of over 200 million auctions per day." To give you a scale comparison, Yahoo! Right Media Exchange claims it sees 10 billion sold impressions per day. 


Ad Exchanges And SSPs

AdBrite CEO Iggy Fanlo discusses the intersection of the sell-side platform and ad exchange models in an opinion piece on MediaPost. He claims that ad exchanges are built around techology (AdBrite runs an ad exchange) and SSPs are built with people and services. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraeeEyIE-5XCxy-3J0w7oVpwe1lcrRU4KhmbRgrj3CCrgNCCG09EaQ9lcGLGep0tJ7x-aRnVcu1qcn2TTArQNf05GAmzcBY1BqozcfFx1iTbtW_hU1Y9Zj3P5xjoGoPxlohKGNHJefnFAjLkFIXmNfiqXz78abUoagvZgicgEOUcbFvQDO0X28Nredde8zpSCsjcoN3PtNH3zj7F4mfQS7c_2v9-RW3YbvVc=> . At times, service seems to be a dirty word for the tech industry as successful exits are based on technology rather than services which are thought to be more easily duplicated. 


Bit.ly's Predictive Analytics

A new deal with Verisign is giving URL-shortener company Bit.ly an eye toward the future as MIT's Technology Review reports, "VeriSign looks up over 50 billion URLs every day and, like Bitly, gets a handle on what people are doing online as a result. In particular, VeriSign's data could add an awareness of activity outside the social sites where Bitly links are used." It's another targeting layer beyond Facebook, Twitter, Google ecosystems. Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraeczb25E2YrgWnGamjOm3mI4lYS57UcSDDiA3eeu_XU_msPzDdgmUgkeEWTUgSmPkuNHdjIHUnvGOzqQxv-s8Ys8By9qovuqkGSDNaZy0_RgjZq5PeYOy9hpU6GeYKsbNGmdGXJH2hoIb7jp6fCJhy_8> . For now, Bit.ly sees reputation management as a key service. 


Ad Spend Sputters

Is ad spending slipping? Kantar Media says that a deceleration of ad spend in TV is underway that has led to a 1.5 % decrease in July and August. September is still being counted. Can automation save the day?? It appears macro-economic factors (recession, war, pestilence) are having some impact. Read more in The Wall Street Journal <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraedXXpmWD_U0CC3ntRkgSS9OCrjy_7d3VBGUBeNLk0y4p9j8_L4UdNMT_KVbJXZqI4VoIk_Z3r3opSkIQ67LZGekjgXgO5ucFAUUzJdFpHa9jwo-I9VEoosF-Wq7mqhgaE_AAvLMkkEdxX4vRFLmCoYUHF8DfFLNYr4L-25aWpkMpyVBOMKIVphA> . There is no mention of how digital trends in particular look, though. 


The Future Of Online Ads

On his Reuters blog, media writer Felix Salmon discusses his AppNexus Summit keynote address last week and says that assumptions by online media people need some pushback. Salmon doesn't see much use for display as he looks at its early days and says, "A few sponsors would buy ads in order to understand the new medium, but there was never anything particularly promising in online banners." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraecB2qu1gZ96F6eOny5xpAQvwx2odkzeVuJNeMMGTUs0-kOR2y1rYbhBD_ydlpX6TbVtx4pVmUW2r2d634Ju2KNOGxicVpzbUpKrOq7rB0E6zhz27saa43cFvQicRf5rnGaz_eumb2oQ6kX6XFFtwV-d6yqH1BtVPWkiKfrMbjVTey-WATkuFqiQCo-CQqoLesM=> .

Procurement Wars

MDC Partners has decided to enter the battle with client-side procurement with one of its own as the agency holding company announced the hiring of Brett Colbert as its chief procurement officer. Colbert used to be global manager of procurement at Anheuser-Busch InBev. Ad Age's Rupal Parekh says Colbert will take part in agency-client negotiations which some see as a battle between price and value.Read more. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraecU_0oMUlPg0yn6ebx6TsEjdoKa59I-r5lkLkUw4wI3gucH1_PY3dkWf7_9UzEq24m3mRcQDGPIomufjZa964MzLgGewTWyp2dvWbv20JyhhZUrhMG5mzEH6NCzDFBxK5b1Ec2NUBGuRQ9WRwU1JAinhIgMHhOcVZFFtdByT3llvNgJeCOVdTKa>  The unspoken wild cards remain automation and innovation which both sides can take advantage of. 


Vote "No" On Consolidation

On Operative's company blog, CEO Mike Leo writes that consolidation is not happening at least if his company's stats are to be believed: "The number of requests to integrate with our platform is three times what they were just two years ago. These numbers and the activity in the space indicate to me, that consolidation is not happening. The reality is that for every company that is bought, two to three are being created, and driving the need for solutions that solve very big problems." Read more on the (Operative's?) Operating System model. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraec-DLqjUF7YN38PMx3vWyWiYrOfrkKJpLZuztF4UbDKrkLNyOYb45wFpu64NRLF8vS8HsgQOJwj3pG4lMLmmbs-bNWwrtG5im_ujIfDqw7Bd0mHhALGtL6EPGjRyvr1YTw-EtO8SFLbyGN40CpxBbgXsg0AhcG-ACFXnyR22ZVy4IbtCDelHRJhwJGrl-eyVQ42DcMxXy2et1gyZOnA67C4>  


The Amazon Library

Amazon is pouring more goodies into its "Prime" product as it progressively becomes a for-pay ($79) loyalty card. You'll now be able to borrow one book a month from Amazon if you own a Kindle Fire. Whoa- Amazon the library! Read more in the Wall Street Journal (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108606909971&s=8442&e=001I_NMUHNraeeeHxzIwq2HaEhvocyKGXIMt_PwfnK9H-sWzJHYKdThNQBcrDbN3QBBJYsheGcJpCqaS6FXP6n3-qfdo3TNBsozANcXd3rnt05h7SBFj37Q_-WR7yhOWn_rmnAPZkFfuGDnUyb6dtdpjKWg_gqUt6YRUN1KZ4QIuodTLUty0JzoN6jgY8lsQcmK> . Unlike some Wall Street analysts who are skeptical about Amazon's investment in the future, JP Morgan analyst Doug Anmuth is jazzed, "We believe Kindle Fire devices and related sales of digital and physical goods on Amazon could drive $5 billion of revenue in 2012 and $8 billion in 2013." Content - in this case, digital books - is a key Amazon asset. Books can be a loss leader for anything people can buy via Ecommerce and Amazon. Walmart can't do that.

Klout And Minors

The New York Times examines Klout and the story of a mother who noticed that her own Klout score - which measures influence across several social media sources - was connected to the Klout score of her son and daughther who had never signed up for the service. She tells the Times, "It freaked me out because these are my kids. (...) It's wrong. They shouldn't be marketing to children." Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiGVqY1-gVgnWXYOoMlyVs2mFjgxBn5FxTTYmASJK7K5LW9ulw2m21ivj7OIlAgdchCiltUxtS8c-p7u888z6fLGGT9CYh8r_-P9l_xKlu5BYUX92N07Xurskq8dhIlzRK6VG2HjUMmYaQkj7xR0nMnyKR4bgQbKaW2ISNUR4vWebUD7--k4pCPSqxrZaFiEbI7gZtBmyv8lrsM-rDYzrx7LZb4Rx3deNkE=> . 


Walmart Vs Amazon

Here's a "did you know?" from Ad Age's Jack Neff: "While Walmart may be 10 times Amazon's size in overall sales, it has only about a tenth as much in online sales, making Walmart a distant also-ran online, even in staples like shampoo and diapers." Neff looks at how Walmart is trying to integrate its online and offline strategies as Ecommerce details are still uncertain. Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiHeSyHQ6zAXh9mfYGBLvu0xPFggCUxFc6MkJLI7kWLgIoa_yzjE38kCtiurwGvQvV5DYVbfRJQ4qiwJKP7bEFXjkjl24iCTaso3D_bguwlSEAwwOPbBMlcateVcHLaOiYnzYwcAWwSNl8hZlBBTLm7FSbMi5Ex_D0CORbWFfEts62_hs5H2Q084avOrXkSZfL8=> . 


Adconion Adds Smartclip

In case you missed it, last week Adconion picked up what it's calling "Europe's leader for digital video advertising" Smartclip to add to its video ad solutions including Joost Media. From the release, "This strategic acquisition will significantly strengthen Adconion's position in online video in its existing markets and accelerate the deployment of its digital distribution platform into the emerging markets of Eastern and Central Europe and into the segment of Connected TV." Read more (PDF) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiG5LalLlbcm_0J3T0e2CRypP1zishKicTRb3HGWAxkPBGLCNfK4pXH-8pFbkmJTluOfIC7KrzkvqUAwhGNQXPaEXIKESgRQy2HAIMKgkxqshXGqhaxpcw17tnSLHu3BZdvAxmuZyZkUYajYQXwZ0gdSwcfKvgLE7QkJ93u_GVPjV0i3wpobJtGPXyYVM9VdduT8kXkPEU8UjQb6hETzTGiS> . 


Crediting Display

Display ad engagement is being tied directly to credit card statements with a new product from Linkable Networks. It seems like a cool idea as The Wall Street Journal's Tom Loftus explains: "After users register a debit or credit card on the Linkable website, they can click on web advertisements tagged with the Linkable logo and have a discount for the advertised item associated with their card. The discount is applied after a purchase is made online or in-store." Linkable can sell against - and retarget against - its cookie pool all day long through exchange-y inventory sources. And, they're not the only ones thinking about this. Read it (subscription) <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiGmi1DMaOlC9ZH1cF3e2Qo4HmBPPk7Ddg1y1pV8duHETTCxWHoJYlZqjuE10AfmtwwyYOWaEDUV1fAg0s7vCEVRTqb4Uk4xKaDhxL1au-QUgH6aggoH9ZKj5FB4QbhtsakZ5PNCIv8-4qVQ2V3GSgsys0NYUmb1ADEFTju08r-nG0rlERHk-gjTpa_Ek5uWN4UC_g9f433rLw==> . 


Mobile Vs PC Display

xAd CMO Craig Hagopian pens a think piece titled "The Keys to Mobile-Display Relevance" on ClickZ. He sees three distinct ways mobile display is different from PC-based display: location, creative and platform. By "platform," he means, "With mobile, you can actually target consumers based on platform: browser, operating system, and device. On the contrary, online display only gives advertisers access to a user's browser type." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiE55l-AlcrBVmXsCyLbiNHCb36fP9lhdkGtEU6J5bMoOKAFeOsIsoKWkLISVapVLJstgQSf1lXrqtdcEtTBW9g7iyLgNq2ftSLTtxuAlYvKpJ-7nn101n9g99sb9AHG4tCOX5BUgD-9it8QZxuYi7qG-K5OIjhqMPnE002GTgrqXD_Wm0nvk9dx> .

About Those Mobile Revenues 

paidContent's Ingrid Lunden interviewed Aol mobile chief David Temkin during last week's Internet Week in London and he told Lunden that "mobile ads running on AOL's 30 free apps and 20 mobile web sites do not yet pay the way for these mobile content forays." Apparently, ages-old deals with telecom carriers to offer AIM instant messenger through SMS is driving the mobile revenue. Read about the legacy revenue <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiHzta2XQkb7qH7WR2Ld3I6fy1cI24i9WvW5JHpp_CUwUKAczkYyI4v9N0GgMQ4T-6uBQofnxmGDx4tW1ob9oLnr9ZOcYw-T1mnMPDU3IVSagsuZPOK8c0kzfWyFCS71H8b3VRuVRItax_il6EnRlzKLm87kHE2NonMrSa0LCRwLbp8fVTE3XFNW6esv3hnGVY2slfAsaOhJ_9o2YCmSpjlnIllIO6mmNCc=> . 


When The Media Plan Attacks!

Josh Dreller brings together a group of agency planners who share their "seven media planning mistakes to avoid" list on iMedia Connection. One planner writes, "The client is often the biggest culprit of this mistake; clients might love seeing ESPN.com on a plan but then balk at a network of sports bloggers because they have never heard of it (and, therefore, assume it's no good)." Go against the grain says the planner! Read 'em all. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108594710306&s=8442&e=0010Smft0PqpiHrsGtDVjzVzwmaWlj9CZcpgXaYLXoBSmJualQyuVL1pJqoV9JXI-i5SOTBECVBqMrXfphImrM3bfVqoONflrTlWt0MsZrWFED2wYXgLO0Q3rjm8uOsWa9yYbJe5rBXGd74jUSXDrsiQedlr2DEEkRsqu-sTlhJEH8=>

Retargeters Banned! 

Schwaaa? All Things D's Peter Kafka says that retargeters are banned on Yahoo!: "People familiar with Yahoo say that this week it told at least three retargeting companies - Criteo, TellApart, and ValueClick's Dotomi - that it would stop selling them its 'Class 2' remnant inventory, which the companies used to purchase on behalf of clients and essentially resell at a premium. The idea, theoretically, is that Yahoo will sell more of those ads itself." The race is on! Will the big portal be able to drive yield without DSP retargeter types? Are MSN and Aol the next to ban retargeters? Read more <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108579935029&s=8442&e=00115dAF3VBkS86rW1K8Ttc89gYCkXAleknXNVs2-VfmE5kwTctEwOZaKzwcqBEKay-ZgmWP5plt9bwRdr1C03miOr8qNO9bas3RBhziu3xBVKlhFhFUJGJzEs945QDMITVKkWPVSvU4iG3wJ9AmD3tZP3jBAczsBAzzOpAQQ1ieAe0jQtc0_XPihjK1fFeDTUA> . 


Digital Appetite?

AppNexus has re-configured its network of vendors as "apps." The company announced its new App marketplace yesterday and the company's head of product, Ari Paparo, told Ad Age's Michael Learmonth, "Our goal with this App marketplace is to present ad tech providers with a new avenue for developing their business that allows them to focus on what they do best -- creating innovative ad technology -- rather than distribution of their offerings." Read it. <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108579935029&s=8442&e=00115dAF3VBkS-KJ9WQFqvZMYj45Pp-9K1sYvXzxp-6K3tikelM5VkM_opcpLRet1hPU4FOEuqCLykhkqCNuELIeGc43FPKkYMRRhyNs104GmgktiktRAwB0CIsqqyYiXSGVqSbBlAqNizq5gIImssuXyPug0lrEKBk_J-GqS3yQV-ogqi4JM83nOQVU8dgRvuVIsaKtmHQgmBMg2Sroe2dHQ==> 


Irish Digital

According to the IAB in Ireland, online advertising grew 20% in the region in the first half of the year "to €65 million and is now the third-largest advertising medium, after print and television." Need more? "Online display advertising grew the strongest, up 41 per cent to €20.7 million, and now accounts for 34 per cent of online spending." Read it <http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?llr=t4t7d7cab&et=1108579935029&s=8442&e=00115dAF3VBkS8v6nJX87osnOycAHKn6DB7wtCR_N54sOQgs7X78pbC8zCGtsaRul1ZcoONcMrs9gh_iFO26NyYEwDysejxVoRQh6kwzyIXQyjO-PZd_BJKNED5OIAq_dOTpdvJ2rNS8Uw_mrmCfjJJm-kBc1SkfI1L5xtx5-MnxOHmnS91WAaHyPUW45nXsB2X> . 


Adding Social

Ad network Brand.net has branched out into social analytics and now says it offers an analytics suite aimed at brand advertisers and provides "insight into the impact of their cross-format digital media campaigns on their social media presence and perceptions."
